## User (2026-04-26 12:09:28)

We are trying to prove the RH, see paper draft attached, along with handovers. Review holistically, then prepare a 6-agent attack plan.

## Assistant (2026-04-26 12:09:33)

I’ll treat the handovers as current state and the TeX draft as the canonical object. I’ll first identify what the draft already contains, then produce a 6-agent plan that avoids duplicating the now-stale local algebra.

_Thought for 1m 1s_

## Holistic verdict

The draft is now correctly positioned as a **local obstruction framework plus an explicit remaining arithmetic gate**, not a completed RH proof. The local order-7/order-9 machinery is valuable, but it has converged to the same obstruction:

\[
A_7^{\mathfrak f}\sim H\Gamma_G,\qquad
A_9^{\mathfrak f}\sim H\Gamma_{G,2},\qquad
H=yq''\sim-\frac{q_0(q'')^3}{288}.
\]

So the live failure mode is not “we need more local algebra.” It is:

\[
q''\approx 0\text{ on }I_\rho
\quad\Longrightarrow\quad
H\approx 0
\]

even while \(\Gamma_G,\Gamma_{G,2}\) remain live. The handovers also correctly warn that projectivization, correction rows, ambient \(D\)-sector rows, and order-11-style higher anisotropy rows are not currently proof-closing because they do not remove the vulnerable source factor. 

The draft’s next attack should therefore be concentrated on the arithmetic statement:

\[
\boxed{
\int_{I_\rho}|q''(m)|^2\,dm\ge Q^{-B}|I_\rho|
}
\]

for the **canonical actual-zeta source curvature**. This is the least nonlinear target left, and it directly attacks the Regime B source-collapse obstruction. The handovers are aligned on this point. 

The most important negative evidence is the same-scale positive packet quadrature model: local zero-side packet geometry can flatten \(q''\) and higher source jets while preserving \(q_0>0\), Gram positivity, and \(\Gamma_G\asymp1\). Therefore the theorem cannot be local/Hadamard-only; it must use actual zeta arithmetic. 

## Strategic priorities

Do **not** spend the main push on order 11, abstract projective bookkeeping, or more correction-row audits. Order 11 is only worth doing as a small no-go audit to confirm the source-divisible tower pattern:

\[
A_{11}^{\mathfrak f}\sim H\Gamma_{G,3}+\text{corrections}.
\]

The main attack should be six coordinated agents:

1. canonicalize \(q''\);
2. test actual zeta numerically;
3. attack zero-side quadrature obstruction;
4. attack prime/AFE fixed-coefficient observability;
5. reintegrate source observability with anisotropy;
6. maintain a kill-or-pivot ledger so the architecture does not drift back into stale local algebra.

---

# 6-agent attack plan

## Agent 1 — Canonical source-curvature object

**Mission:** Make \(q''\) a precise arithmetic object in the draft’s normalization.

**Core question:**

\[
q''_{\rm can}(m)=?
\]

Is it raw phase curvature, source curvature after affine subtraction, whitened/core curvature, or an AFE-normalized observable?

**Tasks:**

1. Locate every definition of \(q,q'',q^{(4)},q_0,I_\rho,Q\), source/core convention, affine subtraction, and whitening convention in the draft.
2. Produce a single canonical definition:

\[
q''_{\rm can}(m).
\]

3. Derive both representations:

\[
q''_{\rm can}(m)=B_2(m)+\sum_\rho K_2(m;\rho),
\]

and

\[
q''_{\rm can}(m)
=
B_2(m)
+
\Re\sum_{n\le X}b_n(\log n)^2 n^{-1/2-im}W(n/T)
+
D_2(m)+E_2(m).
\]

4. Specify \(B_2,P_2,D_2,E_2\), smoothing, dual term, gamma/background contribution, and error scale.

**Deliverable:** A proposition titled:

\[
\textbf{Canonical source-curvature representation.}
\]

**Agent prompt:**

> You are Agent 1: Canonical Source-Curvature Agent. Review the current RH draft and handovers. Your sole task is to make \(q''\) canonical in the paper’s normalization. Identify whether \(q''\) is raw phase curvature, source curvature after affine subtraction, whitened/core curvature, or an AFE-normalized observable. Then derive both the zero-side formula \(q''=B_2+\sum_\rho K_2(m;\rho)\) and the prime/AFE formula \(q''=B_2+\Re\sum b_n(\log n)^2n^{-1/2-im}W(n/T)+D_2+E_2\). Do not attack observability yet. End with exact theorem/proposition text suitable for insertion into the paper, plus a list of unresolved normalization dependencies.

---

## Agent 2 — Actual-zeta numerical observability test

**Mission:** Determine whether the target theorem is numerically plausible for actual zeta, not just surrogates.

**Core measurements:**

\[
\sup_{m\in I}|q''_{\rm can}(m)|,
\qquad
\int_I |q''_{\rm can}(m)|^2\,dm
\]

on intervals

\[
|I|\asymp Q^{-1}
\]

or whatever the draft’s admissible \(I_\rho\) scale resolves to.

**Tasks:**

1. Use Agent 1’s normalization.
2. Design a reproducible computation from actual \(\zeta\), \(Z(t)\), \(\theta(t)\), log-derivatives, or zero data.
3. Scan many \(Q^{-1}\)-scale intervals.
4. Identify whether source-flat intervals occur.
5. Compare actual zeta against:
   - fixed-prime surrogate;
   - AFE surrogate;
   - same-scale packet quadrature model.

**Deliverable:** Numerical evidence table and failure/viability decision.

**Agent prompt:**

> You are Agent 2: Actual-Zeta Numerical Observability Agent. Using the current draft and the canonical \(q''_{\rm can}\) normalization from Agent 1, design and, if feasible, execute numerical tests for actual zeta. Measure \(\sup_I |q''_{\rm can}|\) and \(\int_I |q''_{\rm can}|^2dm\) on admissible intervals \(I\sim Q^{-1}\). Compare actual zeta behavior with fixed-prime/AFE surrogates and the same-scale source-flattening packet model. The goal is to determine whether source-flat intervals are common, rare, or absent. Return formulas, code design/pseudocode, numerical diagnostics, and a clear judgment on whether the observability theorem is plausible.

---

## Agent 3 — Zero-side quadrature obstruction

**Mission:** Attack the same-scale positive packet countermodel.

**Core obstruction:** Local packet geometry permits

\[
q''=q^{(4)}=\cdots=q^{(2M)}=0
\]

while keeping

\[
q_0>0,\qquad g,h>0,\qquad \Gamma_G\asymp1.
\]

Therefore, actual zeta must forbid or fail to approximate the quadrature pattern.

**Tasks:**

1. Formalize the quadrature adversary inside the paper’s zero-packet variables.
2. Quantify how many same-scale packets are required to flatten through order \(2M\).
3. Test possible blockers:
   - zero counting in \(T\pm Q^{-1}\);
   - off-critical zero-density estimates;
   - conjugation and functional-equation quartet constraints;
   - pair correlation/spacing;
   - impossibility of enough same-scale off-line quartets.
4. State a candidate theorem:

\[
\textbf{No same-scale source-flattening quadrature for actual zeta zeros.}
\]

**Deliverable:** Either a credible zero-side obstruction theorem or an explicit reason zero-side data cannot stop the countermodel.

**Agent prompt:**

> You are Agent 3: Zero-Side Quadrature Obstruction Agent. The current draft shows that same-scale positive packet geometry can flatten \(q''\) and higher source jets while keeping \(q_0>0\), Gram positivity, and \(\Gamma_G\asymp1\). Your task is to determine whether actual zeta zeros can realize or approximate this quadrature near a hypothetical off-line packet. Quantify the number, spacing, and off-critical depth of packets needed to flatten \(q'',q^{(4)},\ldots,q^{(2M)}\). Test zero-counting, zero-density, pair-spacing, quartet-symmetry, and same-scale constraints. Produce either a theorem excluding actual-zeta quadrature or a precise statement that zero-side constraints are insufficient.

---

## Agent 4 — Prime/AFE fixed-coefficient observability

**Mission:** Attack the prime-side version as a fixed-coefficient non-approximation theorem.

Once Agent 1 gives

\[
q''_{\rm can}(m)=B_2(m)+P_2(m)+D_2(m)+E_2(m),
\]

source collapse means

\[
P_2(m)\approx -B_2(m)-D_2(m)
\]

throughout \(I_\rho\).

**Tasks:**

1. Treat \(P_2\) as a fixed zeta-coefficient Dirichlet polynomial, not an arbitrary trigonometric polynomial.
2. Investigate localized large-sieve, Montgomery–Vaughan, explicit-formula energy, or uncertainty-principle lower bounds.
3. Try to prove:

\[
\int_{I_\rho}|B_2(m)+P_2(m)+D_2(m)|^2\,dm
\ge Q^{-B}|I_\rho|.
\]

4. If interval estimates fail, formulate the finite-jet nonrecurrence target:

\[
\max_{0\le r\le R}
\left|
(q''_{\rm can})^{(r)}(m_0)
\right|
\ge Q^{-B},
\qquad
R\asymp \frac{\log Q}{\log\log Q}
\text{ or }O(\log Q).
\]

**Deliverable:** Best available prime-side theorem candidate, with clear assumptions and failure modes.

**Agent prompt:**

> You are Agent 4: Prime/AFE Fixed-Coefficient Observability Agent. Work with the canonical representation \(q''_{\rm can}=B_2+P_2+D_2+E_2\). Your task is to prove or disprove a short-interval lower bound \(\int_{I_\rho}|q''_{\rm can}|^2dm\ge Q^{-B}|I_\rho|\) using fixed zeta coefficients. Do not treat \(P_2\) as a generic Dirichlet polynomial with adjustable coefficients. Test localized large sieve, Montgomery–Vaughan mean value, explicit-formula energy identities, and finite-jet nonrecurrence. If a theorem is not reachable, state exactly where generic approximation defeats the method and what fixed-coefficient input would be needed.

---

## Agent 5 — Source/anistropy reintegration

**Mission:** Even if we prove source observability, we still need the original row lower bound or a substitute.

The target row estimate is closer to:

\[
\sup_{m\in I_\rho}
|H(m)|\max(|\Gamma_G(m)|,|\Gamma_{G,2}(m)|)
\ge Q^{-A}.
\]

But source energy alone does not prevent anisotropy from being small exactly where \(q''\) is large.

**Tasks:**

1. Analyze the coupling between \(q''\) and

\[
\Gamma_G=q''-6q_0+2q_0^3,
\]

\[
\Gamma_{G,2}=(1-q_0^2)q''-\frac16q^{(4)}.
\]

2. Find whether source observability plus analytic constraints imply vector observability:

\[
\int_{I_\rho}
|q''|^2\left(\Gamma_G^2+\Gamma_{G,2}^2\right)\,dm
\ge Q^{-A}|I_\rho|.
\]

3. Analyze base-locus regimes:

\[
q''\not\approx0,\quad \Gamma_G\approx0,\quad \Gamma_{G,2}\approx0.
\]

4. Determine whether additional observability is required for \(q_0,q^{(4)}\).

**Deliverable:** A bridge theorem or a clear statement that source observability is necessary but not sufficient.

**Agent prompt:**

> You are Agent 5: Source-Anisotropy Reintegration Agent. Assume the source-curvature observability theorem \(\int_{I_\rho}|q''|^2dm\ge Q^{-B}|I_\rho|\) is true. Determine whether it is enough to recover a source-weighted rank-two lower bound involving \(H\Gamma_G\) and \(H\Gamma_{G,2}\). Analyze possible escape where \(q''\) has mass but \(\Gamma_G,\Gamma_{G,2}\) vanish on the same set. Work with \(\Gamma_G=q''-6q_0+2q_0^3\) and \(\Gamma_{G,2}=(1-q_0^2)q''-\frac16q^{(4)}\). Produce a bridge theorem, vector-valued observability statement, or a precise new missing theorem.

---

## Agent 6 — Kill-or-pivot architecture auditor

**Mission:** Prevent the project from looping back into already-failed branches.

**Tasks:**

1. Maintain the no-go ledger:
   - local row algebra frozen;
   - order 11 low priority;
   - projectivization diagnostic only;
   - correction rows not currently packet-visible/source-robust;
   - ambient \(D\)-sector insufficient unless a new architecture is built.
2. Audit whether any genuinely source-robust row exists outside the current fixed-sector tower.
3. If source observability fails, define the allowed pivots:
   - global projective/affine index theorem;
   - trace/explicit-formula imbalance theorem;
   - genuinely source-robust packet-visible invariant;
   - abandonment of current rank-two norm route.
4. Optionally run a narrow order-11 check only to prove source-divisibility of the tower.

**Deliverable:** Decision tree: continue, pivot, or close the architecture as non-closing.

**Agent prompt:**

> You are Agent 6: Architecture Auditor and Kill-or-Pivot Agent. Your job is not to prove a new theorem directly. Audit the draft and agent outputs to prevent stale attack loops. Maintain a no-go ledger for order-11 algebra, projectivization, correction rows, ambient \(D\)-sector, and generic Euler-product positivity. Determine whether any genuinely source-robust packet-visible invariant remains undiscovered. If the source-curvature observability theorem fails numerically or theoretically, specify the exact allowed pivots: global projective/affine index theorem, trace/explicit-formula imbalance, source-robust row, or abandonment of the rank-two norm route. Optional: do a minimal order-11 source-divisibility audit only if it strengthens the no-go ledger.

---

# Recommended sequencing

Run Agents 1 and 2 first. Agent 1 fixes the object; Agent 2 tests whether the theorem is even plausible. In parallel, Agents 3 and 4 attack the two arithmetic sides: zero-side quadrature exclusion and prime/AFE fixed-coefficient observability. Agent 5 should wait for preliminary outputs from 1, 3, and 4, because reintegration depends on the exact \(q''_{\rm can}\) and the strength of the source lower bound. Agent 6 runs continuously as a guardrail.

The clean success path is:

\[
\text{canonical }q''
\Rightarrow
\int_{I_\rho}|q''|^2\ge Q^{-B}|I_\rho|
\Rightarrow
\text{source/anistropy vector lower bound}
\Rightarrow
\text{rank-two contradiction}.
\]

The clean failure path is:

\[
\text{actual zeta admits source-flat }I_\rho
\Rightarrow
\text{current rank-two norm/projective route is non-closing}.
\]

That is the right bifurcation for the next push.

## Assistant (2026-04-26 12:11:33)

_Thought for 13s_

Below is a detailed shared background brief for all six agents.

---

# Shared Background for All Agents  
## RH proof project — current strategic state

## 0. Executive summary

We are attempting to prove RH through a local rank-two obstruction framework built around packet intervals \(I_\rho\), local jet data, Gram/anisotropy quantities, and fixed-sector coefficient rows.

The proof attempt has reached a clean boundary. The local order-7/order-9 machinery is valuable and should be treated as frozen infrastructure, but it does **not** currently close the proof. Every known norm/projective route collapses on the same quantitative obstruction:

\[
\boxed{
\sup_{m\in I_\rho}
|y(m)q''(m)|
\max\{|\Gamma_G(m)|,\ |\Gamma_{G,2}(m)|\}
\ge Q^{-A}.
}
\]

The problem is the common source factor

\[
H:=yq''.
\]

At leading centered order,

\[
H=yq''
\sim
-\frac{q_0(q'')^3}{288}.
\]

Thus if \(q''\) is small on the relevant packet interval, then \(H\) collapses cubically even when the anisotropy terms are nonzero. This is the central source-collapse vulnerability. 

The next attack should **not** continue generic local algebra, projectivization, correction-row bookkeeping, or order-11 expansion as the main line. The best remaining positive theorem is an arithmetic/source-jet observability statement:

\[
\boxed{
\int_{I_\rho}|q''(m)|^2\,dm
\ge
Q^{-B}|I_\rho|.
}
\]

This theorem must use actual zeta arithmetic. It cannot follow from local packet geometry alone, because same-scale positive packet distributions can make \(q''\) and many higher source derivatives vanish while preserving \(q_0>0\), Gram positivity, and \(\Gamma_G\asymp1\). 

---

# 1. Fixed notation and objects

The main fixed-sector local rows are:

\[
A_7^{\mathfrak f},
\qquad
A_9^{\mathfrak f}.
\]

The first two anisotropy factors are:

\[
\Gamma_G
=
q''-6q_0+2q_0^3,
\]

and

\[
\Gamma_{G,2}
=
(1-q_0^2)q''-\frac16 q^{(4)}.
\]

The common source factor is:

\[
H:=yq''.
\]

At leading centered order,

\[
y_{\rm lead}
=
-\frac{q_0A_2^2}{72},
\qquad
q''=2A_2,
\]

so

\[
\boxed{
H=yq''
\sim
-\frac{q_0(q'')^3}{288}.
}
\]

This cubic dependence is the source of the current obstruction.

The known fixed-sector rows have schematic form:

\[
A_7^{\mathfrak f}\sim H\Gamma_G,
\qquad
A_9^{\mathfrak f}\sim H\Gamma_{G,2}.
\]

More generally, the established fixed-sector tower appears to produce rows of the schematic type:

\[
A_{2k+1}^{\mathfrak f}
\sim
H\Gamma_{G,k}
\]

rather than source-robust rows. No non-source-divisible fixed-sector coefficient row has been identified.

---

# 2. Frozen local theorem stack

Agents should treat the following local results as working infrastructure, not as the next thing to reprove.

The useful qualitative theorem is:

\[
\Gamma_G\ne0
\Longrightarrow
A_7^{\mathfrak f}\ne0.
\]

On the first Gram-isotropy wall,

\[
\Gamma_G=0,
\qquad
\Gamma_{G,2}\ne0
\Longrightarrow
A_9^{\mathfrak f}\ne0.
\]

The order-9 survivor is controlled by a term of the form:

\[
\frac{yq''\Gamma_{G,2}}{128\pi^2g^3}.
\]

This genuinely improves the local detector: order 7 detects first Gram anisotropy, and order 9 detects second Gram anisotropy.

However, this is only **qualitative nonvanishing**. It does not yield the required polynomial lower bound because all known rows still contain \(H=yq''\), and \(H\) may be super-polynomially small if \(q''\) is source-flat.

Agents should not spend the main effort redoing order-7/order-9 algebra.

---

# 3. The two independent failure modes

The current architecture must defeat two separate regimes.

## Regime A — anisotropy collapse, source live

Here:

\[
|H|\asymp1,
\]

but

\[
\Gamma_G\approx0,
\qquad
\Gamma_{G,2}\approx0.
\]

A model bad path is:

\[
q_0=2,
\]

\[
q''=-4+\varepsilon_1,
\]

\[
q^{(4)}=72-18\varepsilon_1-6\varepsilon_2.
\]

Then:

\[
\Gamma_G=\varepsilon_1,
\qquad
\Gamma_{G,2}=\varepsilon_2.
\]

If \(\varepsilon_1,\varepsilon_2\) are super-polynomially small, the anisotropy vector collapses while the source remains live.

This is the regime higher anisotropy rows, such as a hypothetical order-11 row, might address.

## Regime B — source collapse, anisotropy live

Here:

\[
H=yq''\approx0,
\]

while

\[
\max(|\Gamma_G|,|\Gamma_{G,2}|)\asymp1.
\]

For example, tune:

\[
q''=2\varepsilon,
\qquad
\varepsilon=e^{-Q}.
\]

Then:

\[
|yq''|\asymp e^{-3Q}.
\]

Taking

\[
q_0=2,
\qquad
q^{(4)}=0,
\]

gives

\[
\Gamma_G
=
q''-12+16
=
4+O(e^{-Q}).
\]

Thus anisotropy remains live, but the source factor collapses. This is fatal for the current row vector because the known rows are source-divisible.

Regime B is now the dominant obstruction.

---

# 4. Why more local algebra is not the main attack

The known fixed-sector tower has rows modeled by commutator expressions of the type:

\[
X_1YX_{2k}-X_{2k}YX_1,
\]

with

\[
X_1=BS,
\qquad
B\propto q'',
\qquad
Y=yJ.
\]

Projection gives a fixed-sector contribution schematically of the form:

\[
\pi_{\mathfrak f}
\left(
X_1YX_{2k}-X_{2k}YX_1
\right)
=
-2yB(X_{2k})_D I.
\]

Since \(B\propto q''\), these rows are divisible by:

\[
yq''=H.
\]

Increasing the order changes the anisotropy factor \((X_{2k})_D\), but it does not remove the common source factor.

Therefore, an order-11 row would likely look like:

\[
A_{11}^{\mathfrak f}
\sim
H\Gamma_{G,3}
+
\text{corrections}.
\]

That may help against Regime A, but it does not address Regime B. For proof strategy, order 11 is low priority unless used narrowly to confirm the source-divisibility pattern.

---

# 5. Projectivization status

The projective ratio

\[
[A_7:A_9]
=
[\Gamma_G:\Gamma_{G,2}]
\]

formally cancels \(H\). This is useful diagnostically: it shows the direction of the anisotropy vector even when the source factor is small.

But it does not currently close the proof because:

\[
\Gamma_G\approx0,
\qquad
\Gamma_{G,2}\approx0
\]

remains a base-locus problem;

there is no global projective index, winding, holonomy, or endpoint theorem;

correction rows can dominate near \(H=0\);

and the corrections have not been shown to vanish, be absorbable, or be \(H\)-divisible.

Therefore projectivization is presently diagnostic, not proof-closing.

---

# 6. Correction-row status

The correction branch has been audited and does not currently provide a source-robust fixed-sector detector.

The main correction types were:

\[
R_{\rm line},
\qquad
R_{\rm bg/core},
\qquad
R_{\rm norm/sub}.
\]

Current classification:

\[
R_{\rm line}
\]

lies in the \(A_5^{\mathfrak f}\)-reference line. It may be non-\(H\)-divisible, but it is not a certified transverse off-line packet detector.

\[
R_{\rm bg/core}
\]

appears to encode baseline/core/far-tail/gamma analytic data unless a new packet-difference theorem is proved.

\[
R_{\rm norm/sub}
\]

is convention-dependent unless a canonical packet-visible component is isolated.

Thus correction rows currently pollute clean projectivization rather than rescue the proof.

---

# 7. Ambient-sector status

At \(g=h\), an ambient order-7 row survives in the form:

\[
T_7^{(1)}\big|_{g=h}
=
-2yBpD.
\]

This helps against Gram isotropy, but not against source collapse, because again:

\[
B\propto q''.
\]

So this row is still divisible by \(yq''\).

Raw ambient \(J\)-sector rows may contain source-robust information, but exploiting them would require a genuinely new ambient-sector architecture. They are not currently part of the fixed-sector rank-two closure.

---

# 8. Transport-derivative status

If a row has the form

\[
A_j=HG_j,
\]

then a transported derivative gives:

\[
\nabla A_j
=
(\nabla H)G_j+H\nabla G_j.
\]

This only helps if \(\nabla H\) is not small when \(H\) is small.

But because

\[
H\sim-\frac{q_0(q'')^3}{288},
\]

one expects

\[
\nabla H=O((q'')^2)
\]

under good-patch derivative control.

Thus first derivatives reduce cubic source collapse to quadratic source collapse, but finite derivative towers remain vulnerable to finite-order source flattening. Transport does not presently close the source-collapse gap.

---

# 9. Finite and hardened countermodels

The finite \(\xi\)-like countermodel is now strong. It survives:

\[
\text{quartet symmetry},
\]

\[
\text{simple zeros},
\]

\[
\text{same-scale core},
\]

\[
\text{strict core gap},
\]

\[
\text{endpoint separation},
\]

\[
\text{Gram positivity},
\]

\[
\text{Riemann--von Mangoldt-like density},
\]

\[
\text{gamma/background hardening},
\]

\[
\text{integer multiplicity / simple-zero replacement},
\]

and finite explicit-formula constraints.

It can realize:

\[
0<
|yq''|
\max(|\Gamma_G|,|\Gamma_{G,2}|)
<
e^{-Q}
\]

while preserving the current local good-patch constraints.

This proves the present architecture cannot close from local Hadamard-side or local zero-packet constraints alone. A real arithmetic input is required.

---

# 10. Same-scale packet quadrature: decisive local no-go

The strongest local no-go is the same-scale positive packet construction.

A continuous same-scale positive packet distribution on

\[
x^2+c^2=d^2
\]

with density

\[
d\mu(\theta)
=
\frac{2}{\pi}\sin\theta\,d\theta
\]

makes the aggregate packet profile exactly constant near the midpoint:

\[
\int K_{\theta,d}(u)\,d\mu(\theta)
=
\frac1d.
\]

Therefore:

\[
q_\mu^{(r)}(0)=0,
\qquad
r\ge1,
\]

while

\[
q_\mu(0)>0.
\]

By finite quadrature, the continuous positive measure can be replaced by finitely many positive same-scale packets matching derivatives through any finite order. Hence local packet geometry can produce:

\[
q''=q^{(4)}=\cdots=q^{(2M)}=0
\]

while preserving:

\[
q_0>0,
\qquad
g,h>0.
\]

For \(q_0=2\),

\[
\Gamma_G
=
q''-6q_0+2q_0^3
=
4
\]

when \(q''=0\). Thus source collapses while anisotropy remains live.

This is the clearest reason the next theorem must be arithmetic. Local packet positivity, Gram positivity, core-gap openness, and Hadamard-side structure do not rule out source-flatness.

---

# 11. Prime-side / Euler-product status

The Euler product remains the only plausible differentiator between actual \(\zeta\) and hardened finite \(\xi\)-like countermodels.

However, no usable prime-side coercive theorem has been found for the full source-weighted residual:

\[
(yq'')^2(\Gamma_G^2+\Gamma_{G,2}^2).
\]

The problem is that this expression is nonlinear in the local phase jets. The explicit formula is linear; tensorizing it leads to oscillatory multilinear prime sums rather than a sign-definite positive norm.

A hypothetical direct prime-side theorem would need to construct a positive/coercive form:

\[
\mathcal Q_{\rm primes}(m)
\]

such that

\[
\mathcal Q_{\rm primes}(m)
\asymp
(yq'')^2(\Gamma_G^2+\Gamma_{G,2}^2)
+
\text{controlled errors},
\]

and then prove:

\[
\sup_{m\in I_\rho}\mathcal Q_{\rm primes}(m)
\ge Q^{-A}.
\]

No such candidate is currently known.

This is why the narrower target

\[
\int_{I_\rho}|q''|^2
\]

is preferred: it is quadratic in a linear source statistic, not a high-degree nonlinear residual.

---

# 12. Fixed-prime / AFE surrogate evidence

Prior fixed-prime and AFE-style surrogate tests repeatedly found Regime B behavior:

\[
J_2\sim q''\approx0
\quad\text{on }I,
\]

while

\[
J_0\asymp1,
\qquad
g,h>0,
\qquad
R_1\sim\Gamma_G\asymp1.
\]

In one normalized fixed-prime run, the reported pattern was approximately:

\[
\sup_I |J_2|
\approx
5.3\times10^{-3},
\]

\[
\inf_I\max(|R_1|,|R_2|)
\approx
4.49,
\]

and

\[
\sup_I |H|\max(|R_1|,|R_2|)
\approx
4.7\times10^{-9}.
\]

These were surrogates, not actual-zeta computations. But the mechanism survived several hardenings: prime powers, smoothing, dual terms, moving \(\chi\), and exact \(\chi\)-derivatives.

This weakens the hope that generic Euler-product-looking oscillation automatically prevents source-flatness. Actual zeta may still prevent it, but that must be shown with a precise arithmetic theorem.

---

# 13. Prime-log recurrence heuristic

The derivative-flat target is not a single point in a huge torus; it is a finite-codimension analytic tube.

To keep \(q''\) small on an interval of scale:

\[
|I_\rho|\sim Q^{-1},
\]

it may suffice to flatten finitely many derivatives:

\[
(q'')^{(r)}(m_0)\approx0,
\qquad
0\le r\le R,
\]

with roughly

\[
R\asymp \frac{\log Q}{\log\log Q}
\]

or conservatively

\[
R=O(\log Q).
\]

The codimension is then roughly

\[
K\sim R+3.
\]

The expected recurrence cost is heuristically:

\[
Q^{CK}
=
\exp(O((\log Q)^2))
\ll e^Q.
\]

Thus there is no obvious scale-based reason a fixed-prime phase flow cannot hit the derivative-flat tube. To save the architecture through prime phases, one needs a strong fixed-coefficient nonrecurrence theorem, not generic Diophantine optimism.

---

# 14. The exact missing theorem

The current missing theorem is:

\[
\boxed{
\textbf{Off-line-packet source-curvature observability.}
}
\]

A clean target version is:

\[
\boxed{
\int_{I_\rho}|q''(m)|^2\,dm
\ge
Q^{-B}|I_\rho|.
}
\]

A weaker pointwise version is:

\[
\boxed{
\sup_{m\in I_\rho}|q''(m)|
\ge
Q^{-B}.
}
\]

The \(L^2\) version is preferred because it is more compatible with explicit formula, large-sieve, AFE, and uncertainty-principle tools.

This theorem should be interpreted inside the paper’s fixed source/core convention and after canonicalizing \(q''\).

---

# 15. The first required task: canonicalize \(q''\)

Before any agent proves or disproves observability, \(q''\) must be made canonical.

The unresolved question is:

\[
q''_{\rm can}(m)=?
\]

Possibilities include:

\[
\text{raw phase curvature},
\]

\[
\text{whitened/core curvature},
\]

\[
\text{post-affine source curvature},
\]

\[
\text{AFE-normalized observable},
\]

or another normalized object.

The target representation is:

\[
q''_{\rm can}(m)
=
B_2(m)+P_2(m)+D_2(m)+E_2(m),
\]

where:

\[
B_2=\text{background/gamma contribution},
\]

\[
P_2=\text{prime or zero-packet contribution},
\]

\[
D_2=\text{dual/AFE contribution, if applicable},
\]

\[
E_2=\text{controlled error}.
\]

This must be done on both sides:

\[
\text{zero side}
\]

and

\[
\text{prime/AFE side}.
\]

Until this is fixed, “source-curvature observability” is not a precise theorem.

---

# 16. Preferred theorem stack after canonicalization

Once \(q''_{\rm can}\) is defined, the desired theorem stack is:

## Theorem 1 — Canonical source-curvature representation

\[
q''_{\rm can}(m)
=
B_2(m)+P_2(m)+D_2(m)+E_2(m).
\]

This theorem fixes the object.

## Theorem 2 — Off-line-packet source-curvature observability

For every admissible reduced packet interval \(I_\rho\),

\[
\int_{I_\rho}
|q''_{\rm can}(m)|^2\,dm
\ge
Q^{-B}|I_\rho|.
\]

This blocks Regime B in interval-average form.

## Theorem 3 — Source/anistropy reintegration

Source observability alone is not enough. One must still show that \(q''\)-mass cannot concentrate only where anisotropy vanishes.

A possible target is:

\[
\int_{I_\rho}
|q''|^2
\left(
\Gamma_G^2+\Gamma_{G,2}^2
\right)
\,dm
\ge
Q^{-A}|I_\rho|.
\]

Or pointwise:

\[
\sup_{m\in I_\rho}
|H(m)|
\max(|\Gamma_G(m)|,|\Gamma_{G,2}(m)|)
\ge
Q^{-A}.
\]

This is the bridge back to the original rank-two contradiction.

---

# 17. What each agent should assume

All agents should assume:

1. The order-7/order-9 local stack is frozen conditional infrastructure.
2. The known fixed-sector tower is source-divisible unless someone explicitly finds a new source-robust row.
3. Projectivization is diagnostic only unless a global projective index theorem is supplied.
4. Correction rows are not currently certified source-robust packet-visible detectors.
5. Same-scale packet geometry permits source-flatness locally.
6. Actual zeta arithmetic is the only remaining plausible blocker.
7. The primary target is \(L^2\) source-curvature observability on \(I_\rho\).
8. The first technical prerequisite is a canonical formula for \(q''\).

---

# 18. What agents should not do

Agents should not:

\[
\text{redo order-7/order-9 algebra};
\]

\[
\text{continue projectivization without a concrete global index theorem};
\]

\[
\text{treat correction rows as useful without packet-visible/source-robust certification};
\]

\[
\text{attack pointwise } |q''|\ge Q^{-A} \text{ before the } L^2 \text{ theorem};
\]

\[
\text{invoke generic Euler-product positivity};
\]

\[
\text{treat arbitrary Dirichlet-polynomial approximation results as actual-zeta results};
\]

\[
\text{assume local/Hadamard constraints can defeat same-scale source flattening};
\]

\[
\text{make order 11 the main attack}.
\]

---

# 21. Compact one-paragraph handoff

The local rank-two order-7/order-9 theorem is frozen: \(A_7^{\mathfrak f}\sim H\Gamma_G\), \(A_9^{\mathfrak f}\sim H\Gamma_{G,2}\), with \(H=yq''\sim-q_0(q'')^3/288\). This local stack detects anisotropy qualitatively but fails quantitatively if \(q''\) is source-flat on \(I_\rho\). Projectivization cancels \(H\) only formally and lacks a global index theorem; correction rows are not certified source-robust packet detectors; ambient rows remain source-divisible unless a new architecture is built. Finite and hardened \(\xi\)-like countermodels, especially same-scale positive packet quadrature, show that local/Hadamard geometry alone can flatten \(q''\) while keeping \(q_0>0\), Gram positivity, and \(\Gamma_G\asymp1\). Therefore the next attack must be arithmetic: first canonicalize \(q''\) in actual-zeta normalization, then test/prove the off-line-packet source-curvature observability theorem \(\int_{I_\rho}|q''(m)|^2dm\ge Q^{-B}|I_\rho|\). If this fails, the present rank-two norm/projective route is non-closing absent a genuinely source-robust row or a new global projective/trace theorem.

and reserve

for the affine-subtracted complement source.

**Prompt:**

}

try to prove a quantitative ODE rigidity lemma:

\[
\int_I |u|^2\,dm\ge Q^{-B}|I|
\]

plus good-patch analytic bounds implies

\[
\int_I |u|^2(\Gamma_G^2+\Gamma_{G,2}^2)\,dm
\ge Q^{-A}|I|.
\]

Analyze escape scenarios:

1. \(\Gamma_G\) small on most \(u\)-mass;
2. \(\Gamma_G''\) cancels \(2q(q')^2\);
3. \(q\) near \(0\) or \(\pm\sqrt3\);
4. high-frequency oscillation in \(\Gamma_G\);
5. source mass concentrated on tiny subintervals.

Produce either a proof skeleton with exact assumptions or a counterexample model showing the bridge theorem is false under current good-patch hypotheses.

\ge Q^{-B},
\qquad
R(Q)\asymp \frac{\log Q}{\log\log Q}.
\]

1. whether \(m_0\) is arbitrary or tied to a zero-packet equation;
2. whether the off-line packet hypothesis imposes simultaneous constraints on \(F,F',\ldots\);
3. whether zero/prime compatibility yields more equations than free phase recurrence can satisfy;
4. whether \(D_2\) or the \(\chi\)-factor breaks the recurrence heuristic.

Deliver either a stronger nonrecurrence theorem candidate or a precise explanation that recurrence remains plausible even at admissible packet centers.

## Assistant (2026-04-26 12:46:21)

_Thought for 19s_

Read. The new responses are solid, but there is **one important algebra typo** in Agent 6’s proposed LaTeX edits.

## Critical correction

Agent 6’s Edit 5 writes:

```latex
\Gamma_G''
=
u''-6u+12q(q')^2+12q^2u.
```

That coefficient is wrong. Since

\[
\Gamma_G=u-6q+2q^3,\qquad u=q'',
\]

we have

\[
(2q^3)'=6q^2q',
\]

and

\[
(2q^3)''=12q(q')^2+6q^2q''=12q(q')^2+6q^2u.
\]

So the correct identity is:

```latex
\[
\Gamma_G''
=
u''-6u+12q(q')^2+6q^2u.
\]
```

Then the intended formula follows correctly:

\[
\Gamma_{G,2}
=
2q(q')^2-\frac16\Gamma_G''.
\]

This is the highest-priority correction before applying Agent 6’s edits.

---

# Synthesis of the agent responses

The picture is now stable:

1. **Notation is fixed.**  
   The canonical object is the full actual-zeta phase curvature

   \[
   q''_{\can}(m)=q_\zeta''(m)=\Phi_\zeta'''(m),
   \]

   not the affine-subtracted complement curvature

   \[
   q''_{\source,R}(m)=(G^{\new})''(m).
   \]

   Agent 1’s notation cleanup should be applied. The key rule is: keep \(\Gamma_G,\Gamma_{G,2}\) light, but explicitly define them once as canonical full-phase objects unless otherwise decorated. 

2. **Numerics currently support Gate 1.**  
   Agent 2’s canonical zero-side scan found no source-flat intervals. The minimum normalized energy was still order-one:

   \[
   E_I\approx 2.4954,
   \qquad
   B_I^{\rm eff}\approx -0.6817.
   \]

   This supports source-curvature observability, though only as low/medium-height truncated zero-side evidence, not proof. 

3. **Gate 2 is now the key new bridge.**  
   Agent 3 confirms that source observability alone is insufficient. The real bridge is

   \[
   \int_{I_\rho}|q''_{\can}|^2
   \left(\Gamma_G^2+\Gamma_{G,2}^2\right)\,dm
   \ge Q^{-A}|I_\rho|.
   \]

   The ODE identity

   \[
   \Gamma_{G,2}
   =
   2q(q')^2-\frac16\Gamma_G''
   \]

   gives a plausible route, but only with explicit analytic good-patch assumptions: Bernstein/Cauchy bounds, Remez/propagation of smallness, and nonconcentration. Without those, source mass can be hidden on small subintervals. turn11file8

4. **Prime/AFE route remains conditional.**  
   Agent 4 sharpened the arithmetic gate: it should be a **center-conditioned fixed-coefficient finite-jet nonrecurrence theorem**, not generic Dirichlet-polynomial nonrecurrence. The off-line zero condition adds constraints on \(m_0\), but only finitely many; it does not by itself defeat recurrence. No standard prime-side tool closes Gate 1. turn11file9

5. **Global trace is not a shortcut.**  
   Agent 5 found no independent global trace contradiction. A Weil/trace route is possible as a major pivot, but currently it reduces back to fixed-coefficient nonrecurrence or requires a new packet-adapted positivity theorem of RH-level strength. 

6. **Agent 6’s paper edits are mostly right.**  
   Apply them, but fix the \(\Gamma_G''\) coefficient error noted above. Also choose one notation convention consistently: I recommend using

   \[
   q''_{\can}
   \]

   as the displayed object, with a note that \(q''_{\can}=q_{\can}''\) when \(q_{\can}=q_\zeta\).

# Next best attack

The highest-value next agent push is not prime-side recurrence yet. It is:

\[

}

plus polynomial Bernstein/Remez propagation for

# Edit 2 — Add global canonical curvature convention

**Location:** near the start, immediately after:

```latex
\[
q(t):=\Ph'(t).
\]
```

**Insert:**

```latex
\begin{definition}[Canonical actual-zeta phase curvature]
\label{def:canonical-actual-zeta-phase-curvature}
When the local phase is the actual zeta phase, we write
\[
\Ph=\Phi_\zeta,
\qquad
q_\zeta(t):=\Phi_\zeta'(t).
\]
The canonical source-curvature object used by the rank-two Gram rows is
\[
\boxed{
q''_{\can}(m):=q_\zeta''(m)=\Phi_\zeta'''(m).
}
\]
Thus \(q''_{\can}\) is the full actual-zeta phase-derivative curvature in the
same-point Gram normalization.  It is not whitened, projectivized,
AFE-normalized, or affine-subtracted.

When no ambiguity is possible, later centered rank-two formulas may write
\(q,q'',q^{(4)}\) for
\[
q_\zeta,\qquad q''_{\can},\qquad (q_\zeta)^{(4)}.
\]
If a source/core split is being discussed, the complement-source curvature is
instead denoted
\[
q''_{\source,R}(m):=(G^{\new})''(m),
\]
and should not be identified with \(q''_{\can}\) unless a separate rederived
row formula explicitly says so.
\end{definition}
```

# Edit 3 — Clarify \(G^{\new}\) and the complement-source curvature

**Location:** after the sentence:

```latex
This affine absorption is necessary: otherwise the source would contain value
and linear jets and would reopen lower source-grade gates.
```

**Insert:**

```latex
\begin{remark}[Complement-source curvature]
\label{rem:complement-source-curvature-notation}
For the rebuilt source split, define
\[
q''_{\source,R}(m):=(G^{\new})''(m).
\]
Since
\[
r_G(t)=G^{\new}(t)-G^{\new}(m)-G^{\new\,\prime}(m)(t-m),
\]
one has
\[
r_G''(m)=q''_{\source,R}(m).
\]
This is the curvature of the affine-subtracted non-core zero complement.  It is
not the full canonical actual-zeta curvature
\[
q''_{\can}(m)=q_\zeta''(m),
\]
which also includes the core, background, and all remaining completed-phase
contributions in the fixed actual-zeta normalization.
\end{remark}
```

# Edit 4 — Replace the Gram anisotropy definition

**Location:** replace the entire environment:

```latex
\begin{definition}[First and second Gram-anisotropy functionals]
\label{def:gram-anisotropy-functionals}
...
\end{definition}
```

**Replacement:**

```latex
\begin{definition}[First and second Gram-anisotropy functionals]
\label{def:gram-anisotropy-functionals}
On a centered reduced patch, unless explicitly stated otherwise, \(q_0\),
\(q''\), and \(q^{(4)}\) mean the full actual-zeta centered jets
\[
q_0=q_\zeta(m),
\qquad
q''=q''_{\can}(m)=q_\zeta''(m),
\qquad
q^{(4)}=(q_\zeta)^{(4)}(m).
\]
Define
\[
\Gamma_G^{\can}
:=
q''_{\can}-6q_0+2q_0^3 .
\]
For readability we usually suppress the superscript and write
\(\Gamma_G=\Gamma_G^{\can}\).  Then
\[
g-h
=
-\frac{\Gamma_G}{6\pi}.
\]
Thus the Gram-isotropy wall \(g=h\) is equivalently
\[
\Gamma_G=0.
\]

We also define the second Gram-anisotropy functional
\[
\Gamma_{G,2}^{\can}
:=
(1-q_0^2)q''_{\can}-\frac16(q_\zeta)^{(4)}.
\]
Again, when the canonical convention is fixed, we write
\(\Gamma_{G,2}=\Gamma_{G,2}^{\can}\).  This is the anisotropy of the second
centered Gram variation.  In particular, on \(g=h\), the first Gram anisotropy
has vanished, but the second one need not vanish.
\end{definition}
```

# Edit 5 — Replace the opening of the arithmetic source-curvature subsection

**Location:** in:

```latex
\subsection{Arithmetic source-curvature observability: the next attack}
\label{subsec:arithmetic-source-curvature-observability-next-attack}
```

replace the opening paragraph beginning:

```latex
The preceding source-collapse countermodels show that the current rank-two
norm route cannot close ...
```

through:

```latex
This is the positive theorem that would block the interval-local
source-collapse branch.
```

**Replacement:**

```latex
The preceding source-collapse countermodels show that the current rank-two
norm route cannot close from local row algebra, same-scale packet geometry, or
finite Hadamard/quartet symmetry alone.  The first missing input is an
arithmetic source-curvature theorem for actual zeta data.  In the notation
fixed below, the minimal useful pointwise form is
\[
\boxed{
\sup_{m\in I_\rho}|q''_{\can}(m)|\ge Q^{-B}.
}
\]
A stronger and more stable form is the interval energy estimate
\[
\boxed{
\int_{I_\rho}|q''_{\can}(m)|^2\,dm
\ge
Q^{-B}|I_\rho|.
}
\]
This estimate would block the pure source-collapse branch, but it is now only
the first gate.  It does not by itself recover the source-weighted rank-two
lower bound, because the \(q''_{\can}\)-mass could still concentrate near the
anisotropy base locus
\[
\Gamma_G\approx0,
\qquad
\Gamma_{G,2}\approx0.
\]
The second missing input is therefore a source--anisotropy reintegration
theorem, formulated below.
```

# Edit 6 — Replace the canonical representation definition

**Location:** replace the entire current environment:

```latex
\begin{definition}[Canonical source-curvature representation problem]
\label{def:canonical-source-curvature-representation-problem}
...
\end{definition}
```

**Replacement:**

```latex
\begin{definition}[Canonical source-curvature representation problem]
\label{def:canonical-source-curvature-representation-problem}
In this subsection and in every source-observability statement below, the
canonical source-curvature object is
\[
\boxed{
q''_{\can}(m)=q_\zeta''(m)=\Phi_\zeta'''(m).
}
\]
This is the full actual-zeta phase-derivative curvature in the same Gram
normalization used by the local rank-two rows.  It is not the affine-subtracted
complement curvature.  The latter is denoted separately by
\[
q''_{\source,R}(m):=(G^{\new})''(m),
\qquad
G^{\new}=q_{\aux,R}+T_{\far,R}.
\]
The affine-subtracted complement curvature is a component in a chosen
source/core split; it is not the canonical arithmetic object whose nonflatness
is required.

The arithmetic representation problem is to write \(q''_{\can}\) on both sides
of the explicit formula.  On the zero side one needs a representation
\[
q''_{\can}(m)
=
B_2(m)+\sum_{\rho}^{\rm reg}K_2(m;\rho),
\]
with all background, tail, source/core, and regularization conventions fixed.
On the prime/AFE side one needs a representation of the form
\[
q''_{\can}(m)
=
B_2(m)
+
P_2(m)
+
D_2(m)
+
E_2(m),
\]
where
\[
P_2(m)
=
\Re\sum_{n\le X}
b_n(\log n)^2 n^{-1/2-im}W(n/T)
\]
has fixed actual-zeta coefficients, \(D_2\) denotes the dual or
functional-equation contribution, and \(E_2\) denotes a controlled
differentiated error term.  The coefficients \(b_n\), smoothing, dual term,
gamma/background contribution, and error scale must be specified in the same
normalization used by the rank-two local rows.  The point of this convention
is to forbid replacing \(q''_{\can}\) by an arbitrary Dirichlet polynomial or
by the affine-subtracted complement \(q''_{\source,R}\).
\end{definition}
```

---

# Edit 7 — Replace the source-curvature observability hypothesis

**Location:** replace the whole environment:

```latex
\begin{hypothesis}[Off-line-packet source-curvature observability]
\label{hyp:offline-packet-source-curvature-observability}
...
\end{hypothesis}
```

**Replacement:**

```latex
\begin{hypothesis}[Gate 1: off-line-packet source-curvature observability]
\label{hyp:offline-packet-source-curvature-observability}
Let \(I_\rho\) be an admissible reduced good-patch interval attached to a
hypothetical off-line packet \(\rho\).  Actual zeta data satisfy
\[
\int_{I_\rho}|q''_{\can}(m)|^2\,dm
\ge
Q^{-B}|I_\rho|
\]
for some fixed \(B\), outside the already named reduced-base and correction
incidence loci.
Equivalently, in a weaker pointwise form,
\[
\sup_{m\in I_\rho}|q''_{\can}(m)|\ge Q^{-B}.
\]
This is a necessary source-level nonflatness input for the current rank-two
norm route.  It is not sufficient by itself to recover the desired lower bound
for
\[
|H|\max\{|\Gamma_G|,|\Gamma_{G,2}|\}.
\]
\end{hypothesis}
```

# Edit 8 — Insert Gate 2 and the repaired ODE identity

**Location:** immediately after Hypothesis~`\ref{hyp:offline-packet-source-curvature-observability}` and before:

```latex
\begin{remark}[Off-line-packet conditional form]
```

**Insert:**

```latex
\begin{hypothesis}[Gate 2: source--anisotropy vector observability]
\label{hyp:source-anisotropy-vector-observability}
On the same admissible interval \(I_\rho\), actual zeta data satisfy a
source-weighted anisotropy lower bound of the form
\[
\int_{I_\rho}
|q''_{\can}(m)|^2
\left(
\Gamma_G(m)^2+\Gamma_{G,2}(m)^2
\right)\,dm
\ge
Q^{-A}|I_\rho|.
\]
A pointwise substitute would be
\[
\sup_{m\in I_\rho}
|H(m)|
\max\{|\Gamma_G(m)|,|\Gamma_{G,2}(m)|\}
\ge Q^{-A}.
\]
This is a separate gate from
Hypothesis~\ref{hyp:offline-packet-source-curvature-observability}.  Source
curvature may be observable in \(L^2\) while the anisotropy factors are small
on most of the \(q''_{\can}\)-mass.  The current proof architecture requires
both gates, or a single stronger theorem implying both.
\end{hypothesis}

\begin{remark}[ODE form of the reintegration problem]
\label{rem:ode-form-source-anisotropy-reintegration}
Let
\[
u=q''_{\can},
\qquad
\Gamma_G=u-6q+2q^3,
\qquad
\Gamma_{G,2}=(1-q^2)u-\frac16q^{(4)}.
\]
Differentiating \(\Gamma_G\) gives
\[
\Gamma_G''
=
u''-6u+12q(q')^2+6q^2u.
\]
Since \(u''=q^{(4)}\), one obtains the identity
\[
\boxed{
\Gamma_{G,2}
=
2q(q')^2-\frac16\Gamma_G''.
}
\]
Thus the reintegration gate is not merely a prime-side arithmetic problem.  It
also has a local analytic/ODE formulation: source mass for \(u=q''_{\can}\)
must be prevented from concentrating on a set where both
\[
\Gamma_G\approx0
\qquad\text{and}\qquad
2q(q')^2-\frac16\Gamma_G''\approx0.
\]
A proof of Hypothesis~\ref{hyp:source-anisotropy-vector-observability} must
control this base-locus regime, including possible cancellation between
\(\Gamma_G''\) and \(2q(q')^2\).
\end{remark}
```

# Edit 9 — Replace the off-line conditional form remark

**Location:** replace the whole environment:

```latex
\begin{remark}[Off-line-packet conditional form]
\label{rem:offline-packet-conditional-source-observability}
...
\end{remark}
```

**Replacement:**

```latex
\begin{remark}[Off-line-packet conditional form]
\label{rem:offline-packet-conditional-source-observability}
A more targeted version of
Hypothesis~\ref{hyp:offline-packet-source-curvature-observability} uses the
hypothetical off-line packet itself.  Write
\[
q''_{\can}=q''_P+q''_{\mathrm{rest}},
\]
where \(q''_P\) is the contribution of the distinguished off-line packet and
\(q''_{\mathrm{rest}}\) is the contribution of all remaining actual-zeta data:
other core packets, auxiliary/tail terms, background, dual terms, and
controlled errors in the fixed convention.  This \(q''_{\mathrm{rest}}\)
should not be confused with the affine-subtracted complement curvature
\(q''_{\source,R}=(G^{\new})''\) unless the source/core split has explicitly
identified the two.

The interval observability claim may be sharpened to
\[
\int_{I_\rho}|q''_P(m)+q''_{\mathrm{rest}}(m)|^2\,dm
\ge
Q^{-B}|I_\rho|.
\]
Equivalently, the rest term cannot satisfy
\[
q''_{\mathrm{rest}}(m)=-q''_P(m)+O(Q^{-B})
\]
throughout the packet interval.  This formulation uses the off-line-packet
hypothesis directly and is stronger than a generic short-interval lower bound
for \(q''_{\can}\).  The same-scale source-flattening construction shows that
this cannot be proved from arbitrary positive same-scale packet geometry
alone; it must use actual-zeta arithmetic or a restriction on how actual zero
packets may be arranged around \(\rho\).
\end{remark}
```

# Edit 10 — Replace the prime-side observability remark

**Location:** replace the whole environment:

```latex
\begin{remark}[Prime-side observability formulation]
\label{rem:prime-side-source-curvature-observability-formulation}
...
\end{remark}
```

**Replacement:**

```latex
\begin{remark}[Prime-side observability formulation]
\label{rem:prime-side-source-curvature-observability-formulation}
After fixing the representation in
Definition~\ref{def:canonical-source-curvature-representation-problem}, the
source-curvature problem becomes a short-interval fixed-coefficient
non-approximation problem.  Writing
\[
q''_{\can}(m)=B_2(m)+P_2(m)+D_2(m)+E_2(m),
\]
source collapse means
\[
P_2(m)\approx -B_2(m)-D_2(m)
\quad\text{throughout }I_\rho,
\]
up to the controlled error \(E_2\).  The desired arithmetic theorem is
therefore an observability estimate of the form
\[
\int_{I_\rho}|B_2(m)+P_2(m)+D_2(m)|^2\,dm
\ge Q^{-B}|I_\rho|,
\]
with \(E_2\) absorbed into the final error budget.

This is not a generic Dirichlet-polynomial problem.  The coefficients in
\(P_2\) are fixed by the actual zeta/AFE normalization.  Standard localized
large-sieve, Montgomery--Vaughan, explicit-formula energy, or uncertainty
principles are useful diagnostics, but no theorem currently proves this
fixed-coefficient lower bound.  If interval estimates remain out of reach, the
equivalent finite-jet formulation below is the sharper arithmetic target.
\end{remark}
```

---

# Edit 11 — Replace the finite-jet arithmetic remark

**Location:** replace the whole environment:

```latex
\begin{remark}[Finite-jet version of the arithmetic problem]
\label{rem:finite-jet-source-nonflatness-problem}
...
\end{remark}
```

**Replacement:**

```latex
\begin{remark}[Finite-jet version of the arithmetic problem]
\label{rem:finite-jet-source-nonflatness-problem}
The interval energy estimate may also be attacked through finite jets.  On an
interval
\[
I_\rho=[m_0-c/Q,m_0+c/Q],
\]
source collapse requires simultaneous smallness of
\[
\partial_m^r q''_{\can}(m_0),
\qquad
0\le r\le R,
\]
where the scale audit gives
\[
R\asymp \frac{\log Q}{\log\log Q}
\]
or more conservatively \(R=O(\log Q)\).  In an AFE model this becomes a finite
system
\[
\partial_m^r\bigl(B_2+D_2+P_2\bigr)(m_0)
\approx0,
\qquad
0\le r\le R,
\]
or equivalently
\[
P_2^{(r)}(m_0)
\approx
-\left(B_2+D_2\right)^{(r)}(m_0).
\]
The positive theorem would be a fixed-coefficient prime-log derivative-jet
nonrecurrence statement:
\[
\max_{0\le r\le R}
\left|
\partial_m^r q''_{\can}(m_0)
\right|
\ge Q^{-B}.
\]
The recurrence heuristics developed above suggest that this is a difficult
arithmetic theorem and may be false in fixed-prime or AFE surrogates.  It is
therefore not currently proved by large-sieve or generic
Dirichlet-polynomial approximation estimates.
\end{remark}
```

# Edit 12 — Insert Gate 2 into the candidate-route ledger

**Location:** inside:

```latex
\begin{remark}[Status ledger for candidate routes]
\label{rem:status-ledger-candidate-routes}
```

insert the following item **after** the existing item about interval \(L^2\) / source-curvature observability and **before** the global trace / projective index item.

**Insert:**

```latex
\item \emph{Source--anisotropy reintegration.}
Even if the interval source-curvature estimate
\[
\int_{I_\rho}|q''_{\can}(m)|^2\,dm\ge Q^{-B}|I_\rho|
\]
is proved, it does not by itself imply the source-weighted rank-two lower
bound.  One still needs to exclude concentration of \(q''_{\can}\)-mass near
\[
\Gamma_G=0,
\qquad
\Gamma_{G,2}=0.
\]
Equivalently, the architecture needs the vector estimate
\[
\int_{I_\rho}
|q''_{\can}|^2
(\Gamma_G^2+\Gamma_{G,2}^2)\,dm
\ge Q^{-A}|I_\rho|.
\]
The identity
\[
\Gamma_{G,2}
=
2q(q')^2-\frac16\Gamma_G''
\]
turns this into a local analytic/ODE rigidity problem coupled to the arithmetic
source-observability problem.  This bridge is currently a missing theorem, not
a consequence of source observability alone.
```

# Edit 13 — Replace the current branch decision remark

**Location:** replace the whole environment:

```latex
\begin{remark}[Current branch decision]
\label{rem:current-branch-decision-source-collapse}
...
\end{remark}
```

**Replacement:**

```latex
\begin{remark}[Current branch decision]
\label{rem:current-branch-decision-source-collapse}
The current local rank-two architecture should be treated as conditional
infrastructure rather than a proof engine.  The next proof-closing branch is
not additional local row algebra, not order eleven by itself, and not clean
projectivization alone.  The sharp remaining fork is:

\begin{enumerate}
\item Prove actual-zeta source-curvature observability,
\[
\int_{I_\rho}|q''_{\can}(m)|^2\,dm\ge Q^{-B}|I_\rho|,
\]
and then prove source--anisotropy reintegration,
\[
\int_{I_\rho}
|q''_{\can}|^2(\Gamma_G^2+\Gamma_{G,2}^2)\,dm
\ge Q^{-A}|I_\rho|;
\]

\item or construct/verify an actual-zeta source-collapse model satisfying
\[
0<
\sup_{m\in I_\rho}
|yq''_{\can}|
\max\{|\Gamma_G|,|\Gamma_{G,2}|\}
<Q^{-A};
\]

\item or find a genuinely source-robust packet-visible row/invariant not
divisible by \(H=yq''_{\can}\);

\item or prove a global projective/holonomy/trace/index theorem that gives a
contradiction without a local norm lower bound.
\end{enumerate}

Absent one of these, the present rank-two norm/projective architecture remains
a strong local obstruction framework but not a proof of RH.
\end{remark}
```

# Edit 14 — Replace the terminal status conclusion

**Location:** in:

```latex
\begin{remark}[Terminal status of the current architecture]
\label{rem:terminal-status-current-architecture}
```

replace item 6 and the closing paragraphs beginning:

```latex
\item The same-scale source-flattening construction shows ...
```

through the end of the remark.

**Replacement:**

```latex
\item The same-scale source-flattening construction shows that finite
same-scale positive packet geometry does not itself prevent source collapse.
Consequently, an actual proof must use information not already present in the
local Hadamard/quartet packet geometry.  The next positive target is not another
local row identity, but the two-gate chain
\[
\int_{I_\rho}|q''_{\can}(m)|^2\,dm
\ge Q^{-B}|I_\rho|
\]
followed by
\[
\int_{I_\rho}
|q''_{\can}(m)|^2
(\Gamma_G(m)^2+\Gamma_{G,2}(m)^2)\,dm
\ge Q^{-A}|I_\rho|.
\]
The first estimate is source-curvature observability.  The second is
source--anisotropy reintegration.  The second does not follow formally from
the first.
\end{enumerate}

Thus the current framework should be treated as a precise local obstruction
and diagnostic architecture.  To turn it into a proof of \(\RH\), one still
needs at least one genuinely new input:
\[
\boxed{
\text{Gate 1: actual-zeta source-curvature observability}
}
\]
together with
\[
\boxed{
\text{Gate 2: source--anisotropy vector observability,}
}
\]
or else a single stronger theorem implying both.  Alternatively, one needs
\[
\boxed{
\text{a source-robust row/invariant not divisible by }H=yq''_{\can},
}
\]
or
\[
\boxed{
\text{a global projective/affine/trace theorem with correction control.}
}
\]
Absent one of these inputs, the present architecture is conditionally
non-closing.  The least nonlinear arithmetic attack remains
Hypothesis~\ref{hyp:offline-packet-source-curvature-observability}; the most
important bridge is
Hypothesis~\ref{hyp:source-anisotropy-vector-observability}, with the ODE
identity recorded in
Remark~\ref{rem:ode-form-source-anisotropy-reintegration}.
\end{remark}
```

# Final notation policy after these repairs

After applying the above, the paper’s convention is:

\[
q''_{\can}=q_\zeta''=\Phi_\zeta'''
\]

is the full actual-zeta curvature used by the Gram rows;

\[
q''_{\source,R}=(G^{\new})''
\]

is the affine-subtracted complement-source curvature;

\[
q''_{\mathrm{rest}}
\]

or \(q''_R\) in a full decomposition is the rest of \(q''_{\can}\), not automatically the complement-source curvature;

\[
\Gamma_G,\Gamma_{G,2}
\]

may remain undecorated after Definition~\ref{def:gram-anisotropy-functionals}, because that definition explicitly fixes them as canonical full-phase objects unless otherwise stated.

\begin{remark}[What would be needed to save the norm route]
\label{rem:needed-source-jet-nonflatness-theorem}
A necessary new input is actual-zeta source-curvature observability, for
example
\[
\boxed{
\int_{I_\rho}|q''_{\can}(m)|^2\,dm\ge Q^{-B}|I_\rho|.
}

selection, strict core gap, endpoint separation, Gram positivity, finite

such cancellation.

## Assistant (2026-04-26 13:29:16)

_Thought for 12s_

The agent responses now give a clean conditional Gate 2 proof architecture.

## Main update

Gate 2 is no longer vague. It decomposes into four concrete analytic lemmas:

\[
\text{Gate 1}
\quad
\int_{I_\rho}|q''_{\can}|^2\,dm\ge Q^{-B}|I_\rho|
\]

plus:

1. **Source-mass thickening**  
   Gate 1 plus a polynomial Lipschitz bound for

   \[
   u=q''_{\can}
   \]

   gives a polynomially long interval \(J\subset I_\rho\) where

   \[
   |u|\ge Q^{-C}.
   \]

2. **Remez/Bernstein propagation**  
   If

   \[
   \int_J(\Gamma_G^2+\Gamma_{G,2}^2)\,dm
   \]

   is tiny and \(q\) has derivative bounds through order six, then on a smaller polynomially long interval \(J'\),

   \[
   |\Gamma_G|+|\Gamma_{G,2}|+|\Gamma_G''|
   \]

   is tiny.

3. **ODE base-locus rigidity**  
   On a polynomially long interval, one cannot have simultaneously

   \[
   |u|\ge Q^{-C_0}
   \]

   and

   \[
   |\Gamma_G|+|\Gamma_{G,2}|+|\Gamma_G''|\le Q^{-C_2}
   \]

   once \(C_2\) is large enough. The key estimate is:

   \[
   \varepsilon
   \ge
   c\,\frac{\delta^3\ell^2}{3+M^2}.
   \]

4. **Derivative complexity through order six**  
   The draft has ingredients, but not yet a packaged theorem proving

   \[
   \sup_{I_\rho^\ast}|q_\zeta^{(r)}|\le Q^{C_r},
   \qquad 0\le r\le6.
   \]

   This is now the main missing good-patch bookkeeping lemma. 

## Strongest conclusion

Assuming those four pieces, Gate 1 implies Gate 2 with polynomial loss:

\[
\int_{I_\rho}|q''_{\can}|^2\,dm\ge Q^{-B}|I_\rho|
\]

implies

\[
\int_{I_\rho}
|q''_{\can}|^2(\Gamma_G^2+\Gamma_{G,2}^2)\,dm
\ge Q^{-A}|I_\rho|.
\]

Agent 5’s integration proof is sound. The remaining mathematical burden is not the final transfer; it is proving the four component lemmas, especially the order-six derivative complexity package. 

## Important technical guard

The thickening interval must satisfy

\[
J\subset I_\rho
\]

or at least have polynomial overlap with \(I_\rho\). If thickening only produces \(J\subset I_\rho^\ast\) with no controlled overlap with \(I_\rho\), the Gate 2 lower bound over \(I_\rho\) does not follow.

Agent 5 caught this correctly. Keep that guard in all future statements.

## Paper status

Agent 6 found remaining repair-only edits. These are mostly stale text replacements:

\[
H=yq'' \rightsquigarrow H=yq''_{\can},
\]

and replacing “source-jet nonflatness alone” with the two-gate package:

\[
\int |q''_{\can}|^2
\quad+\quad
\int |q''_{\can}|^2(\Gamma_G^2+\Gamma_{G,2}^2).
\]

No further conceptual paper rewrite is needed before the next math push.

## Next math priority

The best next attack is:

\[
\boxed{
\text{prove derivative complexity through order six for }q_\zeta
\text{ on }I_\rho^\ast.
}
\]

Specifically:

\[
\sup_{I_\rho^\ast}|q_\zeta^{(r)}|\le Q^{C_r},
\qquad 0\le r\le6.
\]

This should be attacked by decomposing

\[
q_\zeta=B_\zeta+q_{\core}+T_{\far}
\]

and proving polynomial bounds for:

\[
B_\zeta^{(r)},\qquad q_{\core}^{(r)},\qquad T_{\far}^{(r)}
\]

for \(0\le r\le6\).

The likely missing piece is the finite-order shell estimate:

\[
\sup_{I_\rho^\ast}|T_{\far}^{(r)}|
\ll
\sum_{\rho\notin\mathcal L}\Delta_\rho^{-(r+2)}
\ll Q^{C_r},
\qquad 0\le r\le6.
\]

Once that is packaged, Gate 2 becomes conditionally close.

## Agent 1 / A — Full derivative-complexity proof through order six

You are Agent 1 / A.

Attack the derivative-complexity package needed for Gate 2.

Goal:

\[
\sup_{m\in I_\rho^\ast}|q_\zeta^{(r)}(m)|\le Q^{C_r},
\qquad 0\le r\le6.
\]

Use the local decomposition:

\[
q_\zeta=B_\zeta+q_{\core}+T_{\far}.
\]

Analyze each component separately:

\[
B_\zeta^{(r)},\qquad q_{\core}^{(r)},\qquad T_{\far}^{(r)},
\qquad 0\le r\le6.
\]

Tasks:

1. Prove polynomial bounds for the gamma/background term \(B_\zeta\).
2. Prove polynomial bounds for the finite core, assuming core denominators stay polynomially separated from zero on \(I_\rho^\ast\).
3. Prove or reduce the finite-order far-tail estimate:

   \[
   \sup_{I_\rho^\ast}|T_{\far}^{(r)}|
   \ll
   \sum_{\rho\notin\mathcal L}\Delta_\rho^{-(r+2)}
   \ll Q^{C_r},
   \qquad 0\le r\le6.
   \]

4. Identify exactly which assumptions are needed on:
   - core size;
   - core separation;
   - tail cutoff;
   - local zero-counting;
   - tube width.

Deliverable:

A mathematical proof or sharp conditional theorem for derivative complexity through order six. No paper edits.

---

## Agent 2 / B — Finite-order far-tail shell estimate

You are Agent 2 / B.

Focus only on the far-tail estimate needed by Agent 1.

Goal: prove, for \(0\le r\le6\),

\[
\sup_{m\in I_\rho^\ast}|T_{\far}^{(r)}(m)|
\ll
\sum_{\rho\notin\mathcal L}\Delta_\rho^{-(r+2)}
\ll Q^{C_r}.
\]

Here \(\Delta_\rho\) is the distance from the tail zero \(\rho\) to the local interval/tube.

Tasks:

1. Write the exact one-zero or one-quartet kernel derivative bound:

   \[
   |K_\rho^{(r)}(m)|\ll_r \Delta_\rho^{-(r+2)}
   \]

   or correct the exponent if the kernel normalization gives a different power.

2. Decompose tail zeros into dyadic shells:

   \[
   2^j R\le \Delta_\rho<2^{j+1}R.
   \]

3. Use the available zero-counting input to bound shell occupancy.
4. Sum the shell series through \(r=6\).
5. Determine whether the estimate is polynomial for all admissible choices of tail cutoff \(R\).
6. Identify the weakest tail cutoff condition needed.

Deliverable:

A rigorous shell-sum estimate or a precise obstruction showing the current zero-counting input is too weak. No paper drafting.

---

## Agent 3 / C — Core-packet denominator and finite-core derivative bounds

You are Agent 3 / C.

Focus only on the finite core \(q_{\core}\).

Goal:

\[
\sup_{I_\rho^\ast}|q_{\core}^{(r)}|\le Q^{C_r},
\qquad 0\le r\le6.
\]

Tasks:

1. Write the exact local kernel form for one core packet.
2. Differentiate it \(r\le6\) times and obtain a bound in terms of the minimum denominator/separation.
3. Translate the good-patch conditions into a lower bound on denominators:

   \[
   \mathrm{denom}_\rho(m)\ge Q^{-C}
   \quad
   \text{for }m\in I_\rho^\ast.
   \]

4. Account for the number of core packets.
5. Determine whether quartet symmetry changes the bound or only improves constants.
6. Check whether the distinguished off-line packet itself causes any singularity on \(I_\rho^\ast\), or whether the reduced good-patch construction keeps it polynomially separated.

Deliverable:

A clean finite-core derivative-complexity proof with explicit dependence on core size and separation. No LaTeX insertions.

---

## Agent 4 / D — Remez/Bernstein propagation under minimal smoothness

You are Agent 4 / D.

The previous propagation argument used \(C^6\) real-variable control. Your task is to sharpen or validate it.

Goal: from

\[
\int_J(\Gamma_G^2+\Gamma_{G,2}^2)\,dm\le Q^{-M}|J|
\]

and derivative complexity through order six, prove on a subinterval \(J'\subset J\):

\[
|\Gamma_G|+|\Gamma_{G,2}|+|\Gamma_G''|
\le Q^{-M/C}.
\]

Tasks:

1. Give a fully real-variable proof using interpolation inequalities only.
2. Check whether order six is really enough, or whether controlling \(\Gamma_G''\) from \(L^2\)-smallness of \(\Gamma_G\) requires \(q^{(7)}\) or \(q^{(8)}\) under some hidden step.
3. Optimize the argument:
   - Can \(J'\) be half of \(J\)?
   - Does it need only polynomial relative length?
   - What exponent loss is unavoidable?
4. Test counterexamples: high-frequency small-amplitude functions with large second derivative. Confirm derivative complexity prevents them.
5. State the cleanest propagation theorem with precise assumptions.

Deliverable:

A rigorous propagation proof or a counterexample to the claimed \(C^6\)-based version. No paper edits.

---

## Agent 5 / E — ODE base-locus rigidity stress test

You are Agent 5 / E.

Stress-test the quantitative ODE base-locus rigidity lemma.

Current claimed lemma:

If on an interval \(J\) of length \(\ell\),

\[
|q|\le M,\qquad |u|\ge\delta,
\]

and

\[
|\Gamma_G|+|\Gamma_{G,2}|+|\Gamma_G''|\le\varepsilon,
\]

then

\[
\varepsilon
\ge
c\frac{\delta^3\ell^2}{3+M^2}.
\]

where

\[
u=q''_{\can},
\]

\[
\Gamma_G=u-6q+2q^3,
\]

\[
\Gamma_{G,2}=2q(q')^2-\frac16\Gamma_G''.
\]

Tasks:

1. Verify the proof line by line.
2. Check whether \(u\) really has fixed sign under the assumptions.
3. Check the step deriving a lower bound for \(|q|\) from \(|f(q)|\), where:

   \[
   f(q)=6q-2q^3.
   \]

4. Test the lemma near:
   - \(q=0\);
   - \(q=\pm\sqrt3\);
   - turning points \(q'=0\);
   - large \(|q|\).
5. Look for a counterexample where \(u\) is bounded below but \(f(q)\) changes sign due to \(\Gamma_G\)-error.
6. If the lemma is correct, give the sharpest exponent form in \(Q\):

   \[
   \varepsilon\ge Q^{-A(C_0,L,C_q)}.
   \]

Deliverable:

A verified proof or a corrected version of the lemma. No LaTeX insertions.

---

## Agent 6 / F — Gate 2 counterexample hunter and package minimizer

You are Agent 6 / F.

You are no longer doing paper repair. Your job is to attack the Gate 2 package adversarially.

Goal: determine whether the four-component analytic package is genuinely sufficient and close to minimal.

The proposed chain is:

1. Gate 1 source energy:

   \[
   \int_I |u|^2\ge Q^{-B}|I|.
   \]

2. Source-mass thickening gives \(J\subset I\) with:

   \[
   |J|\ge Q^{-C}|I|,
   \qquad
   |u|\ge Q^{-C}.
   \]

3. Small Gate 2 energy implies:

   \[
   \int_J(\Gamma_G^2+\Gamma_{G,2}^2)\ll Q^{-M}|J|.
   \]

4. Propagation gives \(J'\subset J\) with:

   \[
   |\Gamma_G|+|\Gamma_{G,2}|+|\Gamma_G''|\ll Q^{-M/C}.
   \]

5. ODE rigidity contradicts this if \(M\) is large.

Tasks:

1. Try to construct counterexamples if any one of the four inputs is weakened.
2. Determine which assumptions are strictly necessary:
   - derivative complexity through order six;
   - source Lipschitz;
   - \(J\subset I\) rather than \(J\subset I^\ast\);
   - \(|q|\le Q^C\);
   - control of \(\Gamma_G''\).
3. Check whether Gate 2 can be proved with fewer assumptions, for example without full \(q^{(6)}\) bounds.
4. Track whether any exponent losses are super-polynomial.
5. Decide if the four-component package is sufficient, excessive, or missing a hidden condition.

Deliverable:

A mathematical verdict: “package sufficient,” “package insufficient,” or “package sufficient but reducible,” with explicit countermodels or proof reasoning. No paper edits.

\item The finite-core lower-transfer branch is now subordinate to the
source-collapse problem.  Earlier formulations reduced it to sampled vector
non-concentration, for example
\[
\mathcal N_k^{\rm align}(m,Q)=\varnothing.
\]
The later audits show that such a theorem must include source-level
nonflatness and source--anisotropy reintegration.  In particular, anisotropy or
vector non-concentration alone cannot control the known rows when
\[
H=yq''_{\can}\approx0.
\]

\item The source-weighted layered route is blocked by source collapse.  The
known order-seven/order-nine rows have the form
\[
A_7^{\mathfrak f}\sim H\Gamma_G,
\qquad
A_9^{\mathfrak f}\sim H\Gamma_{G,2},
\qquad
H=yq''_{\can}.
\]
At leading order,
\[
H\sim-\frac{q_0(q''_{\can})^3}{288}.
\]

\[

\]

q_0(m)\asymp1,\qquad g(m),h(m)>0,\qquad
